Initially I felt I was in the right place when I had tune time install my new stereo and speakers. After a few weeks of constant, and what grew to be louder and louder rattling in the doors, I felt the need to investigate. Both driver and passenger side speakers were installed with just 1 screw. Now I understand that we are in trying times, and construction materials are getting more expensive and harder to find daily....but come on....it was  4 more sheet metal  screws.....I also found it to be a nice touch when I stopped by after the stereo was installed to inquire about how the steering wheel control can be adjusted to change radio stations to ones that have been programmed and not scan up and down, and the response was to ask someone who cares. I know this was in jest, and I enjoy banter, but this was quite unprofessional. I'm not sure why any installer would assume the buyer wants to scan every station between the stations they actually have programmed. Maybe this is the new era of car stereos........still scanning............<//review>

Seem like a very capable and honest shop.  My car alarm was behaving strange.  Periodically, it would not allow the car to start.  I took it in and luckily, the problem occurs.  The owner look at it, and told me immediately, you have a dirty connection at the battery.

<review>With so many sushi spots in the area, deciding all comes down to criteria.  Taru Sushi stands out from the crowd by its small cozy atmosphere, fireplace included, and ambitious portion sizes (and I mean, really, really abundant) of fresh ingredients.

If you go home hungry, you are doing something really wrong and should seek professional help.

The three pillars of sushi -- sashimi, nigiri, and rolls -- are all covered in ways that are similarly plentiful and priced fairly.  Sashimi portions and cuts make it more worthy of being labeled as sashimi steaks, nigiri portions involve multiple bites, and the rolls are no exception!

Over many visits, service is noticeably a total hit that you look forward to returning to or a complete miss that makes you regret having to tip as though it was for service (at sushi prices).  Being a family business, you can easily tell a difference between the owners and hired help.  Focusing on the positive, when it's good -- it's warm, friendly, attentive, while easy going...<//review><response>None</response>< gmap_id>

<Resp>None< /Resp><UserId.>107289617426375099368<//UserId.><Pics>None< /Pics><Name>Jose Ramos</Name>< Text>
Mother's Day Fail.

This place gets one star for the food.  This is a tragedy because if the service was anything near acceptable levels it would have had five stars.  Everything we tasted was excellent.  The problem was we had to celebrate multiple birthdays while we waited for our order.

It took twenty minutes from the time of our reservation for someone to come over and see if we wanted anything to eat.  Another forty minutes later, our appetizers started to arrive.  In the meantime, no checking on us from the wait staff, refilling drinks, no apologies for the delays.

Nothing.

I loved the part when our server came over and asked us if we needed anything else.  Never mind they had not even brought our sushi orders yet.  How brain-dead of a question was that?  Had to remind them multiple times what we were missing.  Complete incompetence across the board.

Sadly, we weren't the only ones experiencing these issues.  The tables to the right and left of us had their orders screwed up as well.  At one table, the couple said "just bill me for the drinks and edamame and we are out of here."  They never received their sushi order.  At the table on the other side of us, they received one order of sushi before us despite the fact we arrived earlier.  After that - nothing.  They also had to remind staff of what they ordered.

I think all of us understand that holidays create excess demand on many restaurants.  This place has been in business long enough to know that you have two choices when that happens.  Either staff up so that you can provide a good dining experience for the folks you place at tables.  Or, close a portion of your dining room to ensure you don't subject your excessive guest count to a negative experience.

Unfortunately, they decided to pack 'em in and let the customers wait.  Let's gain as much $$ as we can and compromise our reputation as a dining establishment in Danville.

Not sure whether this review encourages any of you reading it to look elsewhere, but I encourage you to do so.  While the food was good, it did not make up for the poor service experience and operational incompetence of this restaurant.

We won't be back.< /Text>

<Rate>4</Rate><text>It was the tale of 2 restaurants. I didn't care for the place very much when I walked in. First, unless it's a sports bar I don't care for restaurants with TV. Eating out for me is as much a social event as it is for food,and having to compete with a TV is distracting and takes away from my friends and I enjoying each other. And in such a small place there were 2. So...strike 1.

Strike 2 was the service. It's not that our waitress wasn't friendly. She was very unhappy! And this wasn't just my impression but the 3 of us agreed on this. And yes, I know the Japanese style, having been there and worked for many years in SF's Japantown. This woman wasn't reserved- she was sullen and depressing. And she had to be asked to bring over our napkins and silverware and repeated requests for water. And mind you it was over 90 degrees outside and the restaurant didn't believe in turning on their a.c. much. And is it expecting too much to have the table next to us cleared so we aren't looking at people's leftover food the entire time? The place wasn't busy and it appears that, with it close to closing time, they were going to clear the table with all the others.

So I was thinking 1 star and couldn't wait to leave. Especially after I got my miso soup, which I didn't care for very much. Maybe the region from which this miso soup recipe comes from is different from all the miso soup I have had in the past (a lot). But the broth wasn't as clear as I have had before and it was 'heavy' in taste. It seemed that the miso was much more fermented than what I am used to. Well, for my tastes I wasn't crazy about it.

The saving grace for this restaurant, and the reason I will go back in spite of the negative things above, is the taru special rolls we ordered. They were, indeed, among the best sushi I have ever had. I ordered the 'Volcano' and it was fantastic. Each flavor, the fried spicy tuna, jalapeno, cream cheese, tobiko and green onion were both distinct and blended together in your mouth. So many different sensations! And in spite of how good it was, I may have liked the baked Lion King roll better.

Before I had the sushi I thought there would be no way I would return. But the food really made up for the crappy service and lack of ambiance. I really hope it was just a bad day for our waitress and the next time will be better. And maybe it will be cooler so we could sit outside and not have to see the TV :)

So for the food I give it 5 stars and, for now, will only take off 1 star for the lousy ambiance and service, because I figure most people are more interested in good food than good service.< /text><response>None<//response><pictures>None</pictures><userid>112836515862961261310<//userid><Gmap_id>0x808f8ca99a35a9c5:0xadd58cb751918de< /Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Pete is a great barber and an even better guy. He does a lot in the community, and he runs his shop like a family which shows in the nostalgic, homey atmosphere of the shop. All of the barbers are talented. My personal barber, Mr. Al Jones, recently moved away, but I've gotten cuts from most of the other barbers, and I've never been unhappy with the cut. Pete's by far the best, but he keeps a tight crew. Besides Mr. Al and Pete, Louie is also pretty good with Black hair, but that's not to take away from Mauricio and Cisco. I've seen both of them cut, and Mauricio has cut my hair before and done well. Walk-ins are welcome, but I recommend making an appointment otherwise you'll be waiting a while. This is a great place for anyone looking for a classic barbershop: no gimmicks, no frills, just skills, and plenty of trash talk.</review>

Today was my first time here, I think I got lucky because I hear they are extremely busy but I sat in a chair within a minute. Mauricio paid attention to every detail on how I wanted my hair, he also asked to double check before he made a move. Very quick, friendly and professional. I'm the type to hop around barbershops but Mauricio was so good, I'm going to stick with him.</review>

<Name>Christopher Rogers<//Name>< time>

<resp>{'time': 1520450739798, 'text': "Working with extended warranty companies can be confusing and frustrating for the customer. I thought it would be helpful to explain the process....When you have a problem with your vehicle, as this customer has, the first step is to find out if the warranty company will cover the repair. On this customer's vehicle, he had a shifting issue. We offer our initial inspection on the transmission at no charge. Our initial inspection is to test drive the vehicle, check transmission fluid and scan it. After our initial inspection, we felt it necessary to recommend a pan drop. A pan drop helps to see what is happening inside the transmission. In order to do this step, we have to contact the warranty company. Typically, as in this case, the warranty company wants the customer of the vehicle to authorize any additional diagnosis. They want the customer to take some responsibility in the early steps of the process so that, if we are wrong in our dignosis, the customer has to pay for the diagnostic. Once authorized by the customer, if there is a transmission problem, then the warranty company covers the complete repair, including the diagnostic, less the customer's deductible (based on each individual contract). When we dropped the pan on this vehicle, there was metal throughout. This tells us that the transmission is failing. After contacting the warranty company with our findings, they send their own inspector to review the transmission and make a report. The Inspector has 72 hours to come to the center and review the vehicle. The good news is the Inspector's report confirmed our findings. The warranty company searches for a unit or gives the customer an allowance to use towards the repair of their choice. In this case, rather than using the allotted amount to put towards the repair and getting the job done quicker, the customer elected to use the warranty company's supplied unit which took about 10 days and is out of our control. Once the unit was installed and test driven, there was still a drivability problem. This may have been the original cause of the transmission failure. Unfortunately, extended warranty companies take each problem as a separate issue. They told us that the customer would have to authorize additional diagnostic for us to keep going which in this case, was declined. As a courtesy to Mr. Rogers, the Manager reviewed his 30+ page contract in detail, but could not find anything in the contract that would cover the engine problem. He decided to bring it back for further testing and we decided to not charge him an additional diagnostic fee. We found that he was having a misfire issue. On his authorization, we pulled a spark plug and noted that they were completely worn down. They were the wrong spark plugs for his vehicle. Mr. Rogers acknowledged that he wasn't getting that good of gas mileage. When spark plugs are worn to this point, they can send raw fuel through the exhaust and damage the catalytic converters. He authorized us to replace the spark plugs with Motorcraft OEM plugs, but we told him that we could not guarantee this would fix his issue. After replacing the plugs, we testdrove again. It still had a drivability problem. At this point, we recommended that he have his catalytic converters tested at an exhaust shop as we do not perform this type of work. Fortunately, the warranty company acknowledged the transmission damage and covered it even if the cause of the transmission damage is something they do not cover."}< /resp>< Rate>
1< /Rate>
